=500  \\$aFriedrich Erhard Niedt (1674-1708) was a jurist, music theorist and composer who studied in Jena, resided for a while in Hamburg and then moved to Copenhagen. His musical guide reflects compositional techniques in the era of J. S. Bach. Niedt also published a three-part 'Musicalische Handleitung' (1700, 1706 abd 1717), the third part of which was published by Mattheson

=500  \\$aKeyboard score in manuscript. The first part contains forty numbered pages with dances referring to several Dandrieu compositions from different publications for harpsichord. The second part containing twenty-five unnumbered pages with some dances from Francœur and Rebel's 'Tarsis et Zélie' and 'Pirame et Thisbé' by François Francœur and François Rebel.

=041  \\$afre
=059  \\$avn
=245  \\$a[Contredanses, quadrilles]
=260  \\$aFrance [?]$cafter 1828
=300  \\$a39 pages$b20 blank pages, staffed
=500  \\$aViolin part form dances taken from various nineteenth-century operas premiered at the Opéra, among others Meyerbeer's 'Il crociato in Egitto', Rossini's 'Moisé et Pharaon' and 'Le Siège de Corinthe', and Auber's 'Masaniello'. Other names attributed to some of the dances could be the composer's or even the choreographer's (F. de Hugonet, Mons. E. Sermont, Rigal, Mr. L.de B.). One of the dances possibly derives from Hérold ballet pantomime 'Astolphe et Joconde'.
=500  \\$aThe final page contains a five-bar fragment
=533  \\$aDigitized by iGuana, Spring 2022
=534  \\$aMeyerbeer's 'Il crociato in Egitto' premiered in 1824, Rossini's 'Moisé et Pharaon' in 1827, 'Le Siège de Corinthe' in 1826, Auber's 'Masaniello' in 1828, Hérold's 'Astolphe et Joconde' in 1827.

=500  \\$adigital later version (1725): https://www.e-rara.ch/zuz/content/zoom/9981409
=500  \\$aTaller was born on 24 November 1655 in Rott am Inn, in the shadow of the Benedictine monastery there, which was quite important until secularisation and where he also took his vows on 24 October 1679.  He went to Ingolstadt to study theology and law, then worked in his home monastery as a librarian and administrator of the economy, but also as a preacher for his confreres and the surrounding rural communities.    The practical pastoral ministry seems to have been particularly dear to him.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aBuma, Johannes$d1694 -1756$4aut$96888
=245  \\$aBoere bruiloft, of Het huwelijk van Moddeworst, en Griet Beerdberg
=260  \\$aKnollendam$bs.n.$c1767
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aHighly amusing and very detailed poetical description of a country-wedding, written in rather an indecent language; A farcical play is inserted. Extensive commentaries and some other prose accompany the poem.
=500  \\$aJohannes Buma (Leeuwarden 1694 - Leeuwarden 1756), son of a pharmacist, practised that profession himself for some time, but after his father's death he turned to painting and poetry. De Boere Bruiloft (The Merry Wedding), a satire on various well-known Frisian persons, has a long history: according to the biography that precedes the work, Buma started writing it between the ages of thirty and forty, after which it remained unfinished for sixteen years. At the insistence of friends, he finally completed it. It was only eleven years after his death, when all those involved had died, that the poem was dared to be published to spare the feelings of the dramatis personae still in life.
=500  \\$aBeautiful mezzotint portrait of Buma by R. Jelgerhuis after R. Keyert.
=500  \\$anote in pencil "de koperen platen zijn nooit verschenen", refers to the Koperen Platen (engraved illustrations) mentioned on the title page, but do not appear in the book.

=100  \\$aBidloo, Govert$d1649-1713$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1397888$96890
=245  \\$aBrieven der gemartelde apostelen
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bVisser$c1712
=300  \\$a[xii]-122 pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aReissued several times before Bidloo’s death, the text and plates depict the author’s warning against the seducing power of good food, wine, and other earthly delights. Gruesome suffering shown includes stoning, quartering, beating, burning, and other bodily tortures endured by these saints, as necessary preparation for the next world.
=500  \\$aDramatic engravings of a martyred woman (title page) and the martyred Apostels. Although the plates are not signed, several sources attribute the engravings to the gifted and socially well connected artist, Romeyn de Hooghe (1645–1708). There might have been dissatisfaction with the result because Bidloo writes elsewhere about the artist’s incompetence* and later, the plates for Bidloo’s monumental 'Anatomia humani corporis' (Amsterdam, 1685) were drawn by Gérard de Lairesse (1640–1711), and engraved by Abraham Blooteling (1640–1690) and Peter van Gunst (1659?–1724?).

=100  \\$aGerbert, Martin$d1720-1793$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q66625$96622
=245  \\$aReisen durch Alemannien, Welschland und Frankreich, welche in den Jahren 1759. 1760. 1761 und 1762. angestellet worden
=260  \\$aUlm, Frankfurt, Leipzig$bWohler$c1767
=300  \\$a[xvi]-478-[9]-[18] pages$billustrations, 9 unnumbered pages inserted, some folded
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aSoon after being appointed librarian of the monastery school in St. Blasien, Gerbert was sent on journeys from 1759 to 1762 for further education, which took him to Germany, Italy and France. He collected materials on the history of medieval liturgy and music and on the history of the monasteries and met many important personalities. Since Gerbert was initially entrusted with the administration of the monastery library, he began to study church history. The special object of his investigations became the history of church singing in the Middle Ages. Subsequently, he developed into an important music historian of modern times. His interest in music led to his acquaintance with Christoph Willibald Gluck, who became his friend. In 1760, during his travels, he collected copies of medieval treatises on music history and theory from monastery libraries. In Bologna he became friends with Padre Martini; both exchanged their rich experiences. The first result was the travel report 'Iter Alemannicum'.

=300  \\$bprinted in black and red ink, engraved title page, double-framed layout, music examples, bound in white vellum, bowed covers, illustrations, woodcut initial letters$a[xxiv]-306-[4] pages
=500  \\$aJoannes Hauchin was the second Roman Catholic Archbishop of Mechelen. He initiated the publication of the Pastorale Mechliniense, a collection of forms for the various church celebrations, which appeared in Leuven in 1588. 

=500  \\$aMathias Hovius was the third Roman Catholic Archbishop of Mechelen and presided over implementing the Catholic Reformation in the Spanish Netherlands. Hovius founded a seminary in Mechelen and enlisted the Jesuits to draft a catechism. This Malines Catechism first appeared in 1607. The 1623 version of this catechetical manual would form the basis for religious instruction in all Belgian dioceses until well into the 20th century. 
=500  \\$aSubtitle: "Canons and ecclesiastical rites, which pertain to the administration of the Sacrament and other Pastoral duties daily performed, completed by Ioannis Hauchini. Published by order of the archbishop of Mechelen. Now indeed, by the authority of the Most Reverend and Most Illustrious Mathias Hovius, Archbishop of the same Province, enlarged and revised in many places."

=100  \\$aJorissen, Theodoor$d1833-1889$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1878240$96904
=245  \\$aDe Patriotten te Amsterdam in 1794
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bFunke$c1874
=300  \\$a[xxiii]-196 pages$bmarbled endpapers, linen cover
=500  \\$aAfter the Dutch provinces rebelled in 1568 against their sovereign, the Spanish king Philip II (the Eighty Years' War 1568-1648), they proclaimed the Republic of the Seven United Netherlands in 1581. Under the supreme rule of a stadholder, the republic acquired great political and economic power in the 17th century (the Golden Age). The French invasion in 1794 brought an end to this loose confederation of states.In 1794, the French under general Pichegru came to occupy the Republic, aided by Daendels' Batavian Legion, which consisted of exiled patriots. The Batavian republic was instituted, with an extensive reform programme and many meetings. The significance of the Patriot movement should not be underestimated. From the Orangist side, the Patriots were depicted as exercising shopkeepers or country traitors, because of their collusion with France. Many of the ideas from the French Revolution, such as the unitary state, separation of church and state, equal rights and criticism of slavery were realised during the Batavian Republic.

=100  \\$aBilderdijk, Willem$d1756-1831$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1375186$94900
=245  \\$aBezwaren tegen den geest der eeuw, toegelicht
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHerdingh$c1823
=300  \\$a66 pages
=500  \\$aIsaäc da Costa (1798-1860) was een Amsterdams dichter en historicus. Zijn leraar Hebreeuws, Mozes Lemans, bracht hem in contact met Willem Bilderdijk, wiens leerling hij werd. Hij schreef liederen en politieke poëzie. Zelf meende hij dat zijn levensroeping het bestuderen van theologie, letterkunde en geschiedenis was.
=500  \\$aDa Costa was een conservatief. Zijn bekendste werk is de (geruchtmakende) brochure Bezwaren tegen den geest der Eeuw (1823). In een voor- en nawoord en tien hoofdstukken over diverse onderwerpen bepleit hij een dominantie van het (protestantse) christendom in het openbare leven en betreurt hij de dominantie van de Verlichting. Hij keert zich onder andere tegen het mensenverstand, gecontrasteerd met de openbaring van de bijbel, als scheidsrechter in geschillen; tegen de constitutionele monarchie, de idee van volkssoevereiniteit en regering door en voor de bevolking. Waar de Verlichters in de geschiedenis vooruitgang zien, daar ziet Da Costa achteruitgang.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aWestreenen, W. H. J. van$d1783-1848$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q4015771$96913
=245  \\$aVerhandeling over de uitvinding der boekdrukkunst
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bvan Daalen Wetters$c1809
=300  \\$a[iii]-181-[3] pages
=500  \\$aVan Westreenen started collecting at the age of thirteen, with an interest in the history of printing. He collected old manuscripts and incunabula, as well as coins. Van Westreenen also bought parts of the libraries of his relatives Gerard Meerman (1722-1771) and his son Johan Meerman (1753-1815); the library of the latter was publicly auctioned in 1824, with a large part finding its way abroad and therefore part ending up in the Van Westreenen collection. On his death he left his house and the collections to the State of the Netherlands, which became the basis for the still existing Museum Meermanno-Westreenianum, which contains the second largest collection of incunabula (around 1500) in the Netherlands. Since 2019, the museum is called the "Huis van het Boek".

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aBrossard, Sébastien de$d1655-1730$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1026865$99920
=245  \\$aDictionaire de musique
=246  \1$aDictionnaire de musique
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1705
=300  \\$axii-380 pages$bgilt edges,  leather cover elaborately embossed in gold, marbled endpapers, fold out page, music examples
=500  \\$aGuillo 2021 n° 1703-NN, RISM B-VI p. 180
=500  \\$aSébastien de Brossard (1655-1730) was a Jesuit composer and collector of music
=500  \\$aBeautiful binding, made for the library of the Castle of Choisy-le-Roi (France)
=500  \\$aBuilt by Mlle de Montpensier, the Château de Choisy belonged to the Grand Dauphin, son of Louis XIV, who exchanged it for the Château de Meudon. It was finally bought by Louis XV in 1739 and became one of the royal rare book reserves.
In 1742, the king ordered the creation of a library at the Château de Choisy. This library remained dependent on the Royal Library in Paris. The books intended for it were often taken from the duplicates of the Parisian institution. They are bound in red morocco, with the royal coat of arms, and bear the inscription CHOISY LE ROY on the upper cover.
The library was suppressed in October 1787 and the books were transported to Paris, where they are now scattered in the collections. Some volumes (sold as duplicates?) are in private collections.

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aAltonaischer Gelehrter Mercurius $nvols. 1-7
=260  \\$aAltona$bBurmester$c1763-69
=300  \\$a7 vols.  ([ii]-viii-463+[ii]-viii-438+[ii]-viii-342-[8]+[ii]-viii-414+[ii]-viii-430+[ii]-viii-422+[ii]-viii-422 pages)$bengraved title page, uncut pages
=500  \\$aAltona is the westernmost urban borough of the German city state of Hamburg, on the right bank of the Elbe river. From 1640 to 1864, Altona was under the administration of the Danish monarchy. It became part of the Kingdom of Prussia in 1867. In 1938, the Greater Hamburg Act removed Altona from the Free State of Prussia and merged it with the Free and Hanseatic City of Hamburg. 
=500  \\$aAll volumes have uncut pages
=520  \\$aThis newspaper, which for 24 volumes appeared on a weekly basis, was renamed 'Neuer gelehrter Mercurius' in 1773, 'Neuester Altonaischer gelehrter Mercurius' in 1787. It is one of the most important learned and critical journals of the eighteenth century. In addition to reviews of newly published 'learned writings', it also offers 'notes' and news from the republic of letters.

=100  \\$aSmith, Robert$4aut$96924
=245  \\$aHarmonics$bor The Philosophy Of Musical Sounds
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aCambridge$bBentham$c1749
=300  \\$axvi-292-[13] pages$billustrations, 25 folded pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$afacsimile edition see 05A22
=500  \\$aSmith (1689 - 1768) trained as a mathematician and was Plumian Professor of Astronomy at Cambridge for forty-four years (1716 - 1760). Although his work on harmonics has a mathematical basis, he approaches the problems of tuning keyboard instruments as a musician would. 
=500  \\$a"Music was both Smith's pastime and his other main scientific interest. He was an accomplished performer on several instruments, particularly the violoncello, and possessed a 'correct ear'. In his Harmonics he advocated the mean-tone temperament or method of tuning keyboard instruments. In the same work he contributed to the mathematical theory of music with an extended discussion of equal harmonic intervals." (Geoffrey Canton in the new Oxford DNB)

=500  \\$aEsteban de Arteaga (1747-1798) fue uno de los muchos españoles que, en su condición de jesuitas, fueron expulsados de su país por Carlos III en 1767. Siguiendo a la mayor parte de este numeroso grupo, se estableció en Italia. Allí escribió Le Rivoluzioni del teatro musicale italiano (Bolonia, 1783-8 y Venecia, 1785-6) un extenso ensayo histórico-crítico sobre la ópera y, en general, sobre toda manifestación teatral-musical desde la Edad Media hasta su tiempo.

=041  \\$alat$agre
=100  \\$aEutropius$dafter 310-after 387$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q314694$96926
=245  \\$aBreviarium historiæ romanæ$bcum metaphrasi græca pæanii
=260  \\$aLeiden$bLuchtmans$c1793
=300  \\$aliv-[lxxviii]-772-[88] pages
=500  \\$aEutropius, a Roman historian, was active in the 4th century.His Summary of Roman History (Latin: Breviarium Historiae Romanae) is a ten-chapter compendium of Roman history from its foundation to the short reign of Jovian. The independent value of his Summary is small, but it sometimes fills a gap left by the more authoritative records. It is particularly useful to historians for its account of the First Punic War, as no copy of Livy's original books for that period have survived.
=500  \\$aContains also 'Metafrasi Graeca' by Pænius (Paian translation of the Roman history of Europe) e.a.
=500  \\$aAccording to Ton Koopman this copy could be a "prijsband van een stad" (prize book of a city). A prize book is a book that was given in the 16th-19th century to pupils who performed well at school. This phenomenon, which emerged in the 16th century, spread to Latin schools in the Netherlands in the 17th century. It disappeared in the Netherlands in the middle of the 19th century, but in other countries, such as England, prize books were still awarded deep into the 20th century to secondary school pupils who had achieved remarkably good grades. Such a book is called 'band' because it has a special bookmark of leather or parchment with a supralibros, a stamp in gold leaf of the town or school that financed the book, which makes it easily distinguishable from other books. This copy shows the Coat of Arms of the Dutch city Utrecht.

=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bCovens$bMortier$c1739
=300  \\$a5 vols. ([xxxii]-367-[5]-169-[19]+[ii]-460-[12]+[ii]-443-[17]+[iv]-490-[17]+[viii]-418-[6] pages)$b5 engraved frontispieces, 1 inserted engraving
=500  \\$aCharles de Marguetel de Saint-Denis, seigneur de Saint-Évremond (1613-1703) was a French soldier, hedonist, moralist, essayist and literary critic. After 1661, he lived in exile, mainly in England, as a consequence of his attack on French policy at the time of the Peace of the Pyrenees (1659). He is buried in Poets' Corner, Westminster. He wrote for his friends and  never authorised the printing of any of his works during his lifetime, though Barbin in 1668 published an unauthorised collection. But he empowered Des Maizeaux to publish his works after his death, and they were published in London (2 vols., 1705), and often reprinted. Various writings by Evremond online available, see https://onlinebooks.library.upenn.edu/webbin/book/lookupname?key=Saint%2DEvremond%2C%201613%2D1703

=245  \\$aLiber usualis missæ et officii pro domincis et festis cum cantu gregoriano
=260  \\$aParis; Tournai; Rome$bDesclée$c1939
=300  \\$axxix-[i]-1911-12-14-12-10 pages$bloose page (manuscript)
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe Liber Usualis is a book of commonly used Gregorian chants in the Catholic tradition (11th century), compiled by the monks of the Abbey of Solesmes in France. The Liber was first edited in 1896 by Solesmes Abbot Dom André Mocquereau (1849–1930). Its use has decreased since the Second Vatican Ecumenical Council (opened by Pope John XXIII in 1962), in the constitution on the liturgy (Sacrosanctum Concilium), allowed the local language to be used in Church rites.

=300  \\$a[i]-205 pages$bengraved title page$c4°, oblong

=500  \\$aTitel page: oval vignet illustration after Vincenz Georg Kininger (1767-1851) by Loeser Leo Wolf (1775-1840)
=500  \\$aThis is one of the early German translations/Arrangements, in bilingual vocal score. Dramaturges and translators quickly turned Don Giovanni into a Singspiel with spoken dialogue instead of recitatives, and it was in this form that most German theatre-goers got to know the opera until the middle of the nineteenth century. The very first singing translation, by the Bonn composer Christian Gottlob Neefe, was comparatively true to Da Ponte’s original (Magnus Tessing Schneider, The Original Portrayal of Mozart's Don Giovanni, Routledge, 2022)
=500  \\$aNeefe prepared the first known German adaptation of the opera in 1788 for performances in Mannheim and Bonn in 1789. His adaptation was further revised with scenes added by the local dramaturge Heinrich Gottlieb Schmieder (1763-1815) for performance in Mainz and Frankfurt in 1789, by Friedrich Ludwig Schröder (1744-1816) for Hamburg in late 1789.

=500  \\$aJohann Christian Heinrich Rinck (1770-1846) was a German composer and organist. He studied with Johann Christian Kittel (1732–1809), (a pupil of Johann Sebastian Bach), and eventually became Kantor at the music school in Darmstadt, where he was also a court organist from 1813. He composed prolifically, and an organ primer of his enjoyed wide popularity.

=100  \\$aCésar, Pierre-Antoine$d17..-?1809$4arr$98211
=245  \\$aLes Varietés à la mode :$b17e Suite d'Airs, Ariettes d'Opéra et Opéra comiques, Ariettes italiennes, Romances, Vaudevilles et Duo Arrangés Pour le Clavecin ou le Forte-Piano
=260  \\$aParis$bBoyer$bLe Menu$c1785
=300  \\$a14 pages$bleather back and corners, green paper covers
=500  \\$a"Ces exemples prouvent à quelle fréquence parurent dans les périodiques, à partir des années 1760, des annonces qui proposaient des recueils d’ouvertures, airs et ariettes d’opéras et opéras-comiques, d’airs variés et de pots-pourris destinés aux différents instruments. Il s’agissait de séduire un large public d’amateurs qui aimait à se remémorer des airs connus, en lui offrant une sélection d’œuvres nouvelles et variées, mais faciles à exécuter, et d’instaurer avec lui une forme particulière de convivialité. En témoigne plus d’un titre alléchant, comme Les Variétés à la mode de Pierre-Antoine César, parues de 1783 à 1786, qui réunissaient vingt-quatre suites d’airs arrangés pour clavecin ou piano-forte. Ces transcriptions ne procuraient pas seulement, chez soi ou au concert, le plaisir de la réminiscence. Elles entendaient former le goût de l’amateur et relevaient vraisemblablement d’un système pédagogique pratiqué par les maîtres de musique, qui consistait à arranger une œuvre à l’intention de leurs élèves : ainsi le laissent supposer les nombreuses dédicaces adressées, pendant le règne de Louis XVI, à des membres de la noblesse, à l’instar du 1er Pot pouri [sic] Pour le Clavecin ou Forte Piano que Neveu dédia en 1782 à Mademoiselle de Saint-Cyr, dont il était le professeur."
from Michèle Garnier-Butel, 'Du répertoire vocal à la musique instrumentale : les transcriptions d’airs connus en France dans la seconde moitié du xviiie siècle' in Jean Quéniart, 'Le chant, acteur de l'histoire'.
https://books.openedition.org/pur/48019?lang=en

=059  \\$aorg
=100  \\$aBach, Johann Sebastian$d1685-1750$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1339$94766
=240  \\$aBWV 525-530
=245  \\$aPractische Orgelschule enthaltend Sechs Sonaten für zwey Manuale und durchaus obligates Pedal
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aZürich$bNägeli$c[1815]
=300  \\$a94 pages
=500  \\$aThe organ sonatas, BWV 525–530 by Johann Sebastian Bach are a collection of six sonatas in trio sonata form. Each of the sonatas has three movements, with three independent parts in the two manuals and obbligato pedal. The collection was put together in Leipzig in the late 1720s and contained reworkings of prior compositions by Bach from earlier cantatas, organ works and chamber music as well as some newly composed movements. The sixth sonata, BWV 530, is the only one for which all three movements were specially composed for the collection. When played on an organ, the second manual part is often played an octave lower on the keyboard with appropriate registration. Commentators have suggested that the collection might partly have been intended for private study to perfect organ technique, some pointing out that its compass allows it to be played on a pedal clavichord. The collection of sonatas is generally regarded as one of Bach's masterpieces for organ. The sonatas are also considered to be amongst his most difficult compositions for the instrument.

=500  \\$aEarly edition
=500  \\$aThe Inventions and Sinfonias, BWV 772–801, also known as the Two- and Three-Part Inventions, are a collection of thirty short keyboard compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach (1685–1750): 15 inventions, which are two-part contrapuntal pieces, and 15 sinfonias, which are three-part contrapuntal pieces. They were originally written as "Praeambula" and "Fantasiae" in the Klavierbüchlein für Wilhelm Friedemann Bach, a Clavier-booklet for his eldest son, and later rewritten as musical exercises for his students. The two groups of pieces are both arranged in order of ascending key, each group covering eight major and seven minor keys.

=100  \\$aAdam, Adolphe$d1803-1856$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q189544$96451
=245  \\$aDeux quadrilles, sur les motifs du Postillon de Lonjumeau d'Adolphe Adam par Julien pour piano$bavec Acc. de Violon, Flûte, Flageolet ou Cornet à Piston, ad. Lib: par Marmontel

=500  \\$aengraved title page by and after A. Vialon
=500  \\$aPlate nr 1304 (1)
=500  \\$aLe postillon de Lonjumeau (The postman of Lonjumeau) is an opéra-comique in three acts by Adolphe Adam to a French libretto by Adolphe de Leuven and Léon Lévy Brunswick, and premiered by the Opéra-Comique at the Salle de la Bourse in Paris on 13 October 1836. The opera has become the most successful of Adam's works, and the one by which (apart from his ballet Giselle and his Christmas carol Cantique de Noël) he is best known outside his native France. The opera is known for the difficult aria "Mes amis, écoutez l'histoire" which has been called a test for tenors because of the demanding high D, or D5, at the end of the aria. 
=500  \\$aJulien, musical conductor, the son of a military bandsman, was born on 23 April 1812 at Sisteron in the Basses-Alpes. He was brought up in barracks, was instructed in music by his father, and was admitted to the band as piccolo-player. From 1833 to 1836 he was a pupil of Lecarpentier and Halévy at the Paris Conservatoire, but instead of applying himself to serious study occupied himself with composing dance music. In 1836 he persuaded the manager of the Jardin Turc to allow him to direct some concerts of dance music. His skill as an advertiser combined with the quality of his music to attract large and fashionable crowds. His adaptation as quadrilles of Meyerbeer's ‘Huguenots,’ then new and very popular, was heralded in bombastic paragraphs, and was especially successful. Soon he was known in Paris as the Napoleon of music.

=500  \\$aMercadante's I briganti is an opera (melodramma) in three acts, first performed on 22 March 1836 by the Théâtre-Italien in Paris, with an Italian libretto by Jacopo Crescini based on Schiller's Die Räuber.
=500  \\$aPlate nr. 3333
=500  \\$aPhilippe Musard was a French composer who was crucial to the development and popularity of the promenade concert. One of the most famous personalities of Europe during the 1830s and 1840s, his concerts in Paris and London were riotous (in several senses of the word) successes. Best known for his "galop" and "quadrille" pieces, he composed many of these numbers himself, usually borrowing famous themes of other composers. Musard plays an important role in the development of light classical music, the faculty of publicity in music, and in the role of the conductor as a musical celebrity. He has been largely forgotten subsequent to his retirement in the early 1850s.

=500  \\$aActually an opéra-ballet, premiered in 1778
=500  \\$aPublished by the "Verfasser der Deutschen Textes zur Naumannschen Oper Cora"
=500  \\$aJohann Gottlieb Naumann worked in Dresden, Copenhagen and Stockholm. In Sweden he assisted Kind Gustav III with his opera plans. Naumann composed over 20 operas. 
=500  \\$aAccording to the Preface, this is the first opera Naumann composed in Sweden. It was set to a Swedish translation of a French one act Amphion by Thomas, which was converted to a three act opera. This is a German version.

=561  \\$aFrom the "Nachlass Karl Ernst Naumann, Jena" (ms inside front cover).
Carl Ernst Naumann (15 August 1832 – 15 December 1910) was a German organist, composer, conductor, editor, arranger and musicologist. He is best known now as an arranger and editor of the music of J.S. Bach, Mozart and Mendelssohn. He was a grandson of Johann Gottlieb Naumann.

=100  \\$aHaydn, Joseph$d1732-1809$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7349$94783
=240  \\$aHob.XXII:5
=245  \\$aMesse à 4 voix à 4 voix, avec accompagnement de 2 violons, viola et basse, 2 hautbois, 2 bassons, 2 cors, 2 trompettes, timbales et orgue
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf & Härtel$c1811
=300  \\$a148 pages
=490  \\$aŒuvres de J. Haydn
=500  \\$aThe "Missa Cellensis in honorem Beatissimae Virginis Mariae" in C major by Joseph Haydn, Hob. XXII:5, was originally written in 1766, after Haydn was promoted to Kapellmeister at Eszterháza following the death of Gregor Joseph Werner. The original title as it appears on the only surviving fragment of Haydn's autograph score, that has been discovered around 1970 in Budapest, clearly assigns the mass to the pilgrimage cult of Mariazell, Styria. Until that discovery, the work was known as Missa Sanctae Caeciliae, or in German Cäcilienmesse, a title probably attributed to the mass in the 19th century. Whether the alternative title refers to a performance of the piece by the St. Cecilia's Congregation, a Viennese musician's fraternity, on some St. Cecilia's day (22 November), as has been suggested, remains speculation.

=100  \\$aMozart, Wolfgang Amadeus$d1756-1791$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q254$95341
=240  \\$aKV 620
=245  \\$aPartitur der W. A. Mozart'schen Ouverture zu seiner Oper Die Zauberflöte
=260  \\$aOffenbach am Main$bAndré$c1829
=300  \\$a28-2 pages
=500  \\$aTwo-color print, very rare kind of Urtext print from 1829
=500  \\$aTranslation from the parts of the introduction: "Mozart wrote the Overture to the Magic Flute very precisely, like all his manuscripts, but in such a way that he changed several passages, which is otherwise rarely found in his work, partly in the first draft of the score and partly in the subsequent orchestration of this score. Since, by chance, this instrumentation was written at the same time in a much lighter ink, so that these two types of writing are strikingly different from each other, this manuscript also provides us with the evidence: how Mozart drafted this overture, how he changed it during the first writing of the draft score, how he then orchestrated it and changed it again, and how he finally concluded this work. (...) I have now printed everything that Mozart first wrote down, and changed here and there during his writing, in black ink, but all subsequent work has been printed in red ink, and in general everything has been reproduced most exactly according to the original manuscript. The 3 trombones, which Mozart noted on an extra sheet, are also printed here in the same way."

=100  \\$aKittel, Johann Christian$d1732-1809$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q445696$94879
=245  \\$aXXIV Leichte Choral-Vorspiele für die Orgel
=260  \\$aBonn$aCologne$bSimrock$c1813
=300  \\$a15 pages$bno cover
=500  \\$ais 1813 the year of publication or the plate number? or both?
=500  \\$aJohann Christian Kittel was the last student of Johann Sebastian Bach (and one of his favorites).
"Die Bedeutung Johann Christian Kittels ist vor allem in der Pflege und Weitergabe der Tradition von Bach und seiner Werke zu sehen, zumal er auch als dessen „letzter Schüler“ gilt. Hierbei legte er besonderen Wert auf die musikalische Gestaltung des Gottesdienstes und die Rolle des Orgelspiels. Seinen musikalischen Ehrgeiz verwandte er vor allem auf die Ausarbeitung spielbarer Orgelmusik. In diesem Zusammenhang entstand auch ein dreibändiges Lehrbuch des Orgelspiels, das seinerzeit zu den herausragendsten Werken dieser Art zählte."
https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Christian_Kittel

=100  \\$aClementi, Muzio$d1752-1832$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q193673$95350
=240  \\$aOp. 12, nos. 1-4; Op. 23, nos. 1-3; Op. 8, nos. 1-3; Op. 7, nos. 1 & 3. 
=245  \\$aXII sonates pour le pianoforte
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf & Härtel$c1803
=300  \\$a120 pages$bCardboard binding, marbled cover, manuscript title vignet on front cover, engraved title page$coblong
=490  \\$aŒuvres complettes de Muzio Clementi$v1/17
=500  \\$acollection of famous sonatas
=500  \\$aThe Oeuvres Complettes collection of Clementi’s pianoforte music was published in seventeen volumes by Breitkopf & Hartel of Leipzig between 1803 and 1819. Like the Oeuvres complettes of Mozart and Haydn the same firm had begun to bring out in 1798 and 1800, it was offered on subscription terms (Prdnumeration), but the volumes were also obtainable singly. Breitkopf & Hartel were unable to secure Clementi’s cooperation in the undertaking until the almost constantly travelling composer arrived in Leipzig in June 1804. By then five volumes had already appeared, containing merely inaccurate Nachdrucke of works previously published elsewhere: these volumes, as Clementi was later to write to Breitkopf & Hartel (April 22, 1807), “really made a poor father-author blush”. Clementi spent over two months in Leipzig choosing pieces for the next volume(s), correcting and improving them, and reading the proofs.
=500  \\$aVol. I. July 13, 1803 (the dates of the volumes refer to their first announcements in the Intelligenz- Bldtter of the Allgemeine musikalische Zeitung. Such annonucements were often belated): Op. 12, nos. 1 — 4; Op. 23, nos. 1 — 3; Op. 8, nos. 1 — 3; Op. 7, nos. 1 & 3.

=059  \\$a2S T 2vn vla vc bc
=100  \\$aBoccherini, Luigi$d1743-1805$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q189766$96155
=240  \\$aG.532b
=245  \\$aStabat Mater à trois voix
=260  \\$aParis$bSieber$c1805
=300  \\$a68 pages
=500  \\$aHis Stabat Mater was commissioned in 1781 for the Las Arenas church by his employer, the infant Don Luis. The text is based on a text dating from the thirteenth century and attributed to Jacopone da Todi, which meditates on the suffering of Mary at the crucifixion.

Its first version is based on a soprano voice intimately mixed with the string quintet (two violins, one viola, two cellos) forming a sextet. It is composed of 11 parts and lasts about three quarters of an hour.

The musician took up the score again nearly twenty years later (in 1800), adding an overture (first movement of the symphony op. 35 no. 4 of 1782) and three voices: sopranos and tenor. The orchestra part is not touched despite the number of players. The reworked version corresponds to opus 61 of the musician's catalog.
=500  \\$apublisher's autograph on title page

Fac me plagis vulnerari, Allegro commodo (C minor) -- Quando corpus morietur, Andante lento (F minor/F major)

=041  \\$aeng
=059  \\$aS A T B 2SA2T2B 2fl 2ob 3bsn 2tpt 2hrn timp 3vn 2vla vc org bc
=100  \\$aHandel, George Frideric$d1685-1759$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7302$94765
=240  \\$aAlexander's Feast, HWV 75
=245  \\$aAlexander's Feast, an Ode on Saint Cecilia's Day
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$cc. 1790
=300  \\$a141-[2] pages
=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$vplate nos. 65-67
=500  \\$aHändel's Ode 'Alexander's Feast' (HWV 75) is set to a libretto by Newburgh Hamilton. Hamilton adapted his libretto from John Dryden's ode Alexander's Feast, or the Power of Music (1697) which had been written to celebrate Saint Cecilia's Day. Jeremiah Clarke (whose score is now lost) set the original ode to music.
=500  \\$aThe work describes a banquet held by Alexander the Great and his mistress Thaïs in the captured Persian city of Persepolis, during which the musician Timotheus sings and plays his lyre, arousing various moods in Alexander until he is finally incited to burn the city down in revenge for his dead Greek soldiers. 
=500  \\$aEnoch Hawkens (1793-1847) (07A20 Ex Libris ) was a famous singer (countertenor) in the 1830ies and 1840ies 
=501  \\$a07A20 is bound in with' An Ode or Serenata for the Birth Day of Queen Ann. Composed in the Year 1736'
=504  \\$aContains a List of Subscribers (after page 141).
=561  \\$a07A20 Ex Libris Enoch Hawkins (Plate)
=561  \\$a09L05 Ex Libris A. Bulckington 1798 and another name (ms on flyleaf and verso of tp) 
=590  \\$aThe Words by Dryden, Composed in the Year 1736 by G.F. Handel.
=648  \0$a18th Century (1701-1800)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7015$920899

=100  \\$aMattioli, Pietro Andrea$d1501-c.1577$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q457191$97004
=245  \\$aDel modo di distillare le acque da tutte le piante
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1568 or later
=300  \\$a11 pages$bcontains 6 large (woodcut) illustrations and a printer's mark with snake on the titlepage
=500  \\$aNot clear if this is a first edition or a reprint from 1604.
=500  \\$aPietro Andrea Mattioli was a renowned botanist and physician, and this is attested to by his published works. As Mattioli held a post in the Imperial Court as physician to Ferdinand II, Archduke of Austria, and the Emperor Maximilian II, Holy Roman Emperor, this granted him immense influence. Some of his practice included the frequent testing of the effects of poisonous plants on prisoners in order to popularize his works--no doubt a common practice at the time. Mattioli did not tolerate either rivals or corrections. The naturalists and physicians who dared to disagree or correct him did so at their peril. 
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pietro_Andrea_Mattioli

=245  \\$aEen verzameling van ariaas uyt gezogt uyt diverse operaas in 't Hollands, voor 't clavecimbel, viool en fluit$nvol. 1
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMarkordt$cc. 1780 [?]
=300  \\$a[i]-80 pages
=500  \\$aOne of two such collections known to have existed, see Rudolf Rasch, 'Opera in a different language', Music and the City (Leuven: Leuven UP, 2013), 48: "Two volumes published by the Amsterdam music publisher Siegfried Markordt ... offer an impression of how the airs sounded in Neyts's and Vitzthumb's respective Dutch-language productions. Each volume comprises 80 engraved pages, which are generally subdivided into four-page sections, each with its own imprint. This indicates that these sections were produced and sold as periodical instalments. The airs are presented in what was a highly customary format, that of the continuo song ... All airs of the first volume, and most of the second, are headed with the name of the opera from which they are borrowed. The second volume also has a number of airs for which no operatic connection is given or known. ... The two volumes strongly concentrate on the operas of Neyts's repertoire of 1768 and borrow largely from the same operas ..."
=500  \\$aContains aria's from 'De Kuiper', 'Annette en Lubin', 'Den Koning en den Pagter', Ninette in 't Hof', 'Den waarzegger van het dorp', 'Raton en Rosette', 'Het verlooren Lam', 'Den Soldaat Toovenaar', 'Het Melk-Meysje', 'Den Bedroogen Bailliuw', 'De Boheemster', 'Blasius den Lapper', 'De Chineezen', 'Den gelukkigen Wekker'. 
=500  \\$a'Gegraveertd by J:Turpin, en A:Stechwey, op de Princegraft, het tweede Huys van d'Olieberg S'Hagen.'

=100  \\$aSacchini, Antonio$d1730-1786$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q366727$94759
=245  \\$aŒdipe a Colone. $bOpéra en trois actes
=260  \\$aParis$bImbault$c1787
=300  \\$a235 pages
=500  \\$aAntonio Sacchini was a prolific opera composer who worked in Italy, London and Paris, where he became a favorite of Queen Marie Antoinette. 
=500  \\$aImbault plate number 100, Imbault signature on title page
=520  \\$aThe premiere of Œdipe a Colone, intended to inaugurate the new theatre at Versailles, was not a success, possibly due to the quality of the performances, the staging or the acoustics. Queen Marie Antoinette promised Sacchini a better production at Fontainebleau in the autumn, but the "Affair of the Diamond Necklace" meant she was unable to have her wish. The news that the production was cancelled is said to have hastened the death of the already seriously ill composer on October 9, 1786. Œdipe was given a posthumous performance by the Paris Opera at the Théâtre de la Porte Saint-Martin on February 1, 1787. This time the audience was warmly appreciative and the opera became one of the most popular pieces in the repertoire for several decades, reaching a total of almost 600 performances by 1844.

=100  \\$aBochsa, Nicholas-Charles$d1789-1856$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q251397$97017
=245  \\$aNouvelle méthode de harpe, en deux Parties
=260  \\$aParis$bDufaut$bDubois$cc. 1860
=300  \\$a[iii]-38-255 pages$bgreen leather back, red leather cut-out with owner's name in gilt lettering on front cover, contains a full page engraving of Bochsa with harp, and a fold out plate of a harp wth explanations
=500  \\$aNicolas-Charles Bochsa was a harpist and composer who worked mainly in Paris and London. He was became involved in a forgery in Paris and fled to London to escape prosecution. In 1839 he ran off with opera singer Anna Bishop, the wife of the composer Henry Bishop. Together they toured in North America and Europe. They also went to Australia, where Bochsa died after giving only one concert. Anna Bishop was heartbroken, and commissioned an elaborate tomb for him in Camperdown Cemetery Sydney. His 'Nouvelle méthode' is the first truly comprehensive treatise on harp-playing.
=500  \\$aThe binding matches 09L18 (containing harp music by Benigne Henry, Cousineau and Xavier Desarges) also from the collection of Mme De Villaines.

Dédiée à Son Excellence Monsieur le Comte De Montesquieu Fezensac Grand Chambellan de France, Président du Corps Législatif. Par N.CH. Bochsa Fils, Harpiste de la Musique particuliere de S.M. l'Empereur et Roi, et Membre de la Societé des Arts et de l'amitiée. Œuvre 60

=500  \\$aArrangement for harp from an aria in the French version of 'Die Zauberflöte': Les Mystères d'Isis. 
https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Les_Myst%C3%A8res_d%27Isis :
"Les Mystères d'Isis est une adaptation française de l'opéra La Flûte enchantée de Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. La musique a été arrangée par Ludwig Wenzel Lachnith et le librettiste est Étienne Morel de Chédeville. Le public parisien ne connaît La Flûte enchantée qu'à travers Les Mystères d'Isis, représentés la première fois à Paris le 20 août 1801 à la salle de la rue de Richelieu de l'Académie impériale de musique1. L'adaptation y triompha ensuite : entre 1801 et 1827 l'adaptation fut l'objet de 130 représentations."

=100  \\$aCramer, Johann Baptist$d1771-1858$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q455212$94780

=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bNolting$c18xx

=500  \\$aThe edition is actually by Schott in Mainz (plate number 1442), but a strip of paper mentioning "Noltink, Amsterdam" is pasted onto the imprint on the titlepage. 
=500  \\$aJohann Baptist Cramer was one of the most renowned piano performers of his day. He met Beethoven in Vienna, initiating a mutually rewarding relationship, while renewing his friendship with Haydn. After 1800, he was based almost exclusively in England. Following the successful example of his former teacher Clementi, he also became a successful music publisher in London. His many compositions take second place to his pianistic prowess; Beethoven considered him the finest pianist of the day from the standpoint of pure technical perfection.
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Baptist_Cramer
=500  \\$aCramer's etudes are still considered standard didactic works for piano students.

=100  \\$aHandel, George Frideric$d1685-1759$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7302$94765
=240  \\$aChandos Anthems HWV 250; HWV 256b; HWV 256a; HWV 248; HWV 253; HWV 249b; HWV 251b
=245  \\$aAnthem[s] in Score, Composed at Cannons,$bFor his Grace the Duke of Chandos Between the Years 1718 & 1720
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1790?
=300  \\$a7 vols in 1 (42+32+52+39+59+31+40 pages)
=500  \\$aIn the series 'The Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score', plate nos. 72-77 and 79.
=500  \\$aThis volume contains Anthems I - VI and VIII. Nr. VII is not included. 
=500  \\$aChandos Anthems, HWV 246–256, is the common name of a set of anthems written by George Frideric Handel. These sacred choral compositions number eleven. The texts are psalms and combined psalm verses in English. Handel wrote the anthems as composer in residence at Cannons, the court of James Brydges, who became the First Duke of Chandos in 1719. His chapel was not yet finished, and services were therefore held at St Lawrence in Whitchurch. The scoring is intimate, in keeping with the possibilities there. 
=504  \\$aEach Anthem has it's own printed Table of Contents at the end. 
=505  \\$gContains 7 Anthems in Score: 1. 'I will magnify Thee' [HWV 250, plate 72], 2. 'Let God arise' [HWV 256b, plate 73], 3. 'Let God arise' [HWV 256a,  plate 74], 4. 'Have Mercy upon me O Lord' [HWV 248, plate 75], 5. 'O Come let us Sing unto the Lord' [HWV 253, plate 76], 6. 'O Sing unto the Lord a new song' [HWV 249b, plate 77], 8. 'As pants the Hart for cooling streams' [HWV 251b, plate 79].

=300  \\$a[ii]-250 pages$bleather back, striking (modern?) orange endpapers, portrait as frontispiece, contains 3 pages of illustrations (2 of them are not bound in the volume but loose)
=500  \\$aLouis (originally Ludewig) Spohr was a violinist and a prolific composer, highly regarded in his lifetime. Spohr invented the violin chinrest and the orchestral rehearsal mark. 
=500  \\$aSpohr's Violinschule is a standard work in violin instruction. The first part deals with practical matters like the instrument itself, strings, the bow, keeping the materials in good working order. The second part starts with playing open strings and continues in 66 etudes to an advanced level. All pieces are in duet form so the teacher can play along. The third part deals with musical performance in various settings (from accompaniment to playing solo in a concerto).

=041  \\$afre
=245  \\$aLes quatre fils Aymon.$bHistoiré héroique
=260  \\$aParis$bLebigre$c18xx
=300  \\$a104 pages
=500  \\$aThe Four Sons of Aymon (French: [Les] Quatre fils Aymon, Dutch: De Vier Heemskinderen, German: Die Vier Haimonskinder), sometimes also referred to as Renaud de Montauban (after its main character) is a medieval tale spun around the four sons of Duke Aymon: the knight Renaud de Montauban, his brothers Guichard, Allard and Richardet, their magical horse Bayard, their adventures and revolt against the emperor Charlemagne. The story had a European success and echoes of the story are still found today in certain folklore traditions. 
=500  \\$aThe oldest extant version of the tale is an anonymous Old French chanson de geste, Quatre Fils Aymon, which dates from the late 12th century and comprises 18,489 alexandrine (12-syllable) verses grouped in assonanced and rhymed laisses (the first 12,120 verses use assonance; critics suggest that the rhymed laisses derive from a different poet). It is one of the longest of all the chansons de geste. Other, later versions of the chanson range from 14,300 to 28,000 verses. Of the dozen extant versions of the chanson, all are anonymous except for one, Histoire des quatre fils Aymon, attributed to Huon de Villeneuve, a 13th-century trouvère. The Renaud chansons de geste were transformed into prose romances in the 14th and 15th centuries, and, judging from the number of editions, the prose Quatre Fils Aymon was the most popular romance of chivalry in the late 15th century and first half of the 16th century in France.

The tale is generally included in the Doon de Mayence "cycle" of chansons.

=041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aMaffei, Scipione$d1675-1755$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1587432$96886
=245  \\$aLa Verona illustrata$bridotta in compendio, principalmente per uso de' forestieri, con varie aggiunte. $n1-2/2
=260  \\$aVerona$bMoroni$c1771
=300  \\$a2 vols. (LI-[v]-175+173-[6] pages)$binserted folded plates, bound in cardboard cover
=500  \\$aA monumental work dedicated to the history, writers and monuments of Maffei's city: Verona.
=500  \\$a"Verona illustrated reduced in compendium, mainly for the use of foreigners, with various additions"
=500  \\$aIn the present edition for the use of visitors the first volume contains a biography of Maffei, a history of Verona and a description of the ancient Roman amphitheatre, which is illustrated in six plates. The second volume describes and illustrates in seventeen plates some notable sights of the city and its fortifications, and concludes with a brief survey of its literary history.

=500  \\$aThe work is dedicated by 'P.M.' [identified by the RIBA cataloguer as Pietro Montanari, the editor] to Alvise Mocenigo II, Podestà di Verona (1628-1709)
=500  \\$aFrancesco Scipione Maffei was a Venetian writer and art critic,  an antiquarian with a humanist education, and author of many articles and plays.
=500  \\$aSome plates are signed as made by Dall'Acqua.
=500  \\$aSome plates are copied from the 1732 edition, but others are new, e.g. those of the Museo and the Dogana.

=520  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.

=041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aGaleazzi, Francesco$d1758-1819$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1441041$97091
=245  \\$aElementi teorico-pratici di musica$bcon un saggio sopra l'arte di suonare il violino analizzata, ed a dimostrabili principi ridotta
=246  \1$aElementi di musica
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aRome$bChracas$c1791$bPuccinelli$c1796
=300  \\$a2 vols. (252-[11]+ 316-[7] pages)$bfold-outs, music examples
=500  \\$aFrancesco Galeazzi worked as a violin teacher and for more than a decade as director of the Teatro Valle music theatre in Rome. His two-volume music-theoretical work "Elementi teorico-pratici di musica con un saggio sopra l'arte di suonare il violino analizzata, ed a dimostrabili principi ridotta", is a very important source on, among others, key characteristics, and an important key to understanding the classical musical style; an expanded edition appeared in 1819 and an English translation as early as 1796. It contains the earliest descriptions of the sonata form. In addition to music, Galeazzi was also concerned with mathematics and other sciences, with geography and history. Among Galeazzi's compositions, several duet collections, a collection of string trios and vocal works are known; he also composed an opera.

=500  \\$aSarganeck's  "Die höchstnöthige Berechnung", published in Züllichau in 1735, is added to Schmidt's book of 1736 , in a continuing pagination (p.601-672)
=500  \\$aGeorg Sarganeck was a pedagogue, grammar school teacher, school inspector and pietist. He was born in Dolní Suchá in the Těšín region, a village in Karviná District, Moravian-Silesian Region, Czech Republic. He studied at the University of Halle. From 1728 to 1730 he worked as a teacher at the Evangelical Jesus School in Těšín, from where he was expelled by Emperor Charles VI because of his pietism. He went to Germany, where he taught at schools in Neustadt an der Aisch and Halle. He is one of the most important personalities of Czech non-Catholic exile literature. 
=500  \\$aTitle page of Sarganeck's book: "Die höchstnöthige Berechnung der Sünden-Schulden deren Grösse und Mannigfaltigkeit gegen die unendliche Versöhnung und Liebe Gottes in Christo Jesu. Anfangs bey einem Schul=Examine, Nun aber zu gemeinsamer Erbauung herausgegeben von George Sarganeck, Rectore der hochfl. Brandenburg=Culmbach. Stadt=Schule zu Neustadt an der Aisch."

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aRegt, Jan de$d1665-1715$4aut$97118
=245  \\$aSlegten-tyd, mengeldichten, gezangen, en nacht-wachts, kluchtspel
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bGroot, de$c1733
=300  \\$a[xii]-144 pages$bengraved frontispiece, illustrations
=500  \\$aDedicated to Ludolph Smids, physician, antiquarian and poet. 
=500  \\$aengravings by J. Schijnvoet
=500  \\$aVery little is known about Jan de Regt (1665-1715). He was the eldest son of Michiel Michielsz de Regt, sailmaker, and Lijsbet Jans van Riet, a baker's daughter. The De Regt family lived in the Jordaan where Jan was baptised in the Noorderkerk, and later on the Waal (the Kromme or the Oude, it is not clear). When Jan de Regt registered as a citizen of Amsterdam in 1694, he gave 'merchant' as his profession. This is a vague designation that could indicate anything from shopkeeper to international trader. He was explicitly not a bread-poet, but a leisure poet. His oeuvre is small: occasional poems, a 'In Praise of Amsterdam', a farce (De nachtwachts) and a number of 'Gezangen' (Songs), mostly on everyday subjects, such as 'Knorhanen gegeten' (Roosters eaten), 'Waar schuil ik voor de lonken' (Where do I hide from the ogres), and 'Al 't gedruis aan ons huis' (All the commotion at our house). Those 'Gezangen' were in fact songs, to be sung to then-familiar tunes like 'En de bok sprong op het geitje'. For the song tune of some others, such as the 'Vechtzang' (poem in praise of the Vecht), De Regt refers to the compositions of 'Sr. Andreas Parchem [= Parcham], given name Musician'. Occasionally, his poets' pen lent itself to current affairs, such as the death of Maria Stuart (1695) and the battle of Oudenaarde (1708). Some noise arose after De Regt's long poem Slechten tyd (1711), to which Jan van Gijsen wrote a counter-poem entitled Goeden tyd. A pamphleteer claimed that the gentlemen had entered into a 'war of poets'. But Van Gijsen vehemently disputed that. Never, he argued, 'was I an enemy of De Regt./ That gentleman never harmed me with works nor with words,/ 'I did sin' so 'I said that I ever heard anything to the man's slander./ I know his good behaviour and praise his poetry,/ which is also ten times as good as mine'. De Regt unfortunately kept quiet on the matter. Jan de Regt died as a 'young man' or bachelor in Amsterdam.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aRicchinius, Thomas Augustinus$d1695-1762$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q87193344$97129
=245  \\$aIndex Librorum Prohibitorum Ssmi D. N. Benedicti XIV Pontificis Maximi jussu recognitus, atque editus
=260  \\$aParma$bCarmignani$c1783
=300  \\$a315-12-[2] pages$bengraved frontispiece, 
=500  \\$aRicchini, a learned Italian ecclesiastic, was born at Cremona in 1695. At the age of fifteen he entered the Dominican order, devoted himself to poetry, and published at Milan several religious pieces. He afterwards taught theology in the principal houses of his order in Lombardy, and filled the office of prior at Cremona. Called to Rome in 1740, he became in 1749 secretary of the Congregation of the Index and examiner of the bishops. He worked in the service of the Roman censorship and was part of the commission that published the list of forbidden books (L'Indice) in 1750, as well as the later revisions of 1753, 1758, 1763... He enjoyed the favor of Benedict XIV, who often made use of his learning in literary work. In 1759 Ricchini became one of the masters of the pope's palace. He died at Rome in 1762.

=100  \\$aMarcello, Benedetto$d1686-1739$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q312784$95459
=245  \\$aIl teatro alla moda $bosia Metodo sicuro, e facile per ben comporre, & esequire l'opere italiane in musica all'uso moderno
=260  \\$aVenice$bAldiviva Licante$c1722
=300  \\$a72 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aA discussion and full English translation is published in Musical Quarterly:
Pauly, Reinhard G. (1948). "Benedetto Marcello's Satire on Early 18th-Century Opera". The Musical Quarterly. 34 (2): 222–233. ISSN 0027-4631. JSTOR 739306.
Marcello, Benedetto; Pauly, Reinhard G. (1948). "Il Teatro Alla Moda--Part I". The Musical Quarterly. 34 (3): 371–403. ISSN 0027-4631. JSTOR 739550.
Marcello, Benedetto; Pauly, Reinhard G. (1949). "Il Teatro Alla Moda--Part II". The Musical Quarterly. 35 (1): 85–105. ISSN 0027-4631. JSTOR 739581.
=504  \\$ahttps://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Il_teatro_alla_moda
=520  \\$a'The Fashionable Theater' is a satirical pamphlet in which its author, the Venetian composer Benedetto Marcello, vents his critical opinions on the milieu of the Italian opera seria in the first decades of the eighteenth century. Virtually every aspect of opera seria and its social environment is mercilessly criticized: the artificiality of plots, the stereotyped format of music, the extravagant scenography and machinery, the inability and venality of composers and poets, the vanity and vulgarity of singers, the avidity of impresarios, the ineptitude of musicians. 

The frontispiece contains several allusions to well-known protagonists of the Venetian theater of the time. For instance, the publisher's name "Aldiviva Licante" refers, by means of anagrams, both to Antonio Vivaldi, then very famous as an opera composer, and to the singer Caterina Canteli. The engraving shows a little boat rowed by a well dressed gentleman. Numerous supplies such as a wine barrel and sacks of flour are lying in the forward part of the boat, at the bow of which stands a bear (representing impressario Orsatti) wearing a wig and waving a little flag. An angel wearing a priest's hat and playing on a diminituive violin occupies the opposite position, hovering over the rudder at the stern, representing Antonio Vivaldi. Underneath the picture follows an imprint, in which every word printed in capitals refers to a composer, singer or other person involved in Venetian opera business.
=534  \\$aOriginally published, anonymously, in 1720
=561  \\$aEx libris Abrahao Carvalho (plate) and I. M. Iraham, Rio 1978 (manuscript)
=590  \\$anel quale si danno avvertimenti utili, e necessarj a poeti, compositori di musica, musici dell'uno, e dell'altro sesso, impresarj, suonatory, ingegneri, e pittori di scene, parti buffe, sarti, paggi, comparse, suggeritori, coposti, protettori, e madri di virtuose, ed altre persone appartenenti al teatro. Dedicato dall'autore del libro al compositore di esso. Stampato ne Borghi di Belisania per Aldiviva Licante, all'insegna dell'Orso in Peata. Si vende nella strada del Corallo alla porta del palazzo d'Orlando. Come pure in Milano da Francesco Agnelli.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aEpinay, Louise marquise d'$d1726-1783$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q264254$97132
=245  \\$aMémoires
=260  \\$aParis$bFasquelle$cs.d.
=300  \\$a2 vols. (viii-460+500 pages)
=500  \\$aThe pseudo-memoires of Louise d'Epinay are written in the form of a sort of autobiographic romance, 'L'Histoire de Madame de Montbrillant', begun when she was thirty but never published in her lifetime. It intersperses fictionalized set pieces exhibiting the sensibilité of the earliest generation of Romantics, with genuine letters and autobiographical material. Bequeathed to Baron Grimm, a mangled version of the manuscript was edited by J. P. A. Parison and J. C. Brunet (Paris, 1818) as 'Mémoires et correspondance de Madame d'Épinay' with all the names changed to identify the supposed originals: Madame d'Épinay figures in it as Madame de Montbrillant, and René is generally recognized as Rousseau, Volx as Grimm, Gamier as Diderot, who is sometimes credited with major interventions in the text. The work has had a checkered career since. The only accurate edition is George Roth, ed. Les Pseudo-mémoires de Madame d'Épinay, 3 vols., 1951.
=520  \\$aLouise Florence Pétronille Tardieu d'Esclavelles d'Épinay (1726-1783), better known as Mme d'Épinay, was a French writer, a saloniste and woman of fashion, known on account of her liaisons with Friedrich Melchior, Baron von Grimm, and Jean-Jacques Rousseau, as well as her acquaintanceship with Denis Diderot, Jean le Rond d'Alembert, Baron d'Holbach and other French men of letters during the Enlightenment. She was also one of many women referenced in Simone de Beauvoir's 'The Second Sex' as an example of noble expansion of women's rights during the 18th century.
=561  \\$aEx libris Charles François de Fontanellaz (plate), lived from 1891-1956 and was editor of 'la Revue Automobile'.

=500  \\$aRohr was a Saxon cameralist, natural scientist in the early period of the Enlightenment and, as a writer, one of the best-known authors of German domestic literature. In addition to his cameralistic and scientific publications, he made a lasting name for himself with his two contemporary travel guides for the Upper and Lower Harz Mountains.

=100  \\$aHabermann, Johann$d1516-1590$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q90836$97137
=245  \\$aChristliches Gebet-Buch auf all Tage in der Wochen zu gebrauchen
=260  \\$aBerlin$bLorentz$c1712

=500  \\$aHabermann was a Lutheran theologian, edification writer and Hebraist
=501  \\$aBound in with Crüger's 'Praxis pietatis melica' 
=520  \\$aHabermann's prayer book apportioned for the first time the prayers for various Christian needs among the several days of the week. With a few exceptions the prayers are written in plain Biblical language, without ornament. The work was translated into Latin, English (as The Enimie of Securitie, London, 1580), and French, and was widely circulated in Protestant circles. Despite its occasional crudities of expression the book is still used; and some of the prayers have passed into church books. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1565 as 'Christliche Gebet für alle Not und Stende der gantzen Christenheit'

Nach verschiedenen andern Editionen übersehen und an vielen Orten wieder ersetzet.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aMontesquieu, Charles de Secondat$d1689-1755$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q15975$97138
=245  \\$aLettres persanes
=250  \\$a2nd Ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bs.n.$c1786
=300  \\$a527 pages
=504  \\$aIncludes an index
=520  \\$a'Persian Letters' is a literary work recounting the experiences of two fictional Persian noblemen, Usbek and Rica, who spend several years in France under Louis XIV and the Regency. Lettres persanes was an immediate and durable sensation and was often imitated, but it has been diversely read over time. Until the middle of the twentieth century, it was the "spirit" of the Regency which was largely admired, as well as the caricature in the classical tradition of La Bruyère, Pascal and Fontenelle. No one thought to attach it to the novelistic genre. The Persian side of the story tended to be considered as a fanciful decor, the true interest of the work lying in its factitious "oriental" impressions of French society, along with political and religious satire and critique. In the 1950s began a new era of studies based on better texts and renewed research. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1721

=500  \\$aColley Cibber was an English actor-manager, playwright and Poet Laureate. His colourful memoir describes his life in a personal, anecdotal and even rambling style. His importance in British theatre history rests on his being one of the first in a long line of actor-managers, on the interest of two of his comedies as documents of evolving early 18th-century taste and ideology, and on the value of his autobiography as a historical source.

=260  \\$aLeiden$bHack$c1647
=300  \\$a[xxxix]-850-[82] pages
=500  \\$aGaius Suetonius Tranquillus was a Roman historian who wrote during the early Imperial era of the Roman Empire. His most important surviving work is this set of biographies of 12 successive Roman rulers, from Julius Caesar to Domitian, sometimes also entitled De vita Caesarum. Other works by Suetonius concerned the daily life of Rome, politics, oratory, and the lives of famous writers, including poets, historians, and grammarians. A few of these books have partially survived, but many have been lost.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aAler, Paul$d1656-1727$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q552883$97140
=245  \\$aGradus ad Parnassum, sive Novus synonymorum, epithetorum, phrasium poeticarum, ac versuum thesaurus
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bJanssonius$c1739
=300  \\$a[ii]-747 pages
=500  \\$aThe Latin phrase Gradus ad Parnassum, "steps to Parnassus", became famous when Jesuit Paul Aler (1656–1727), a schoolmaster, published in 1687 anew an earlier Thesaurus attributed to Pierre Joulet, sieur de Chastillon (1545–1621). This was not a general dictionary but a thesaurus of synonyms, epithets, verses and phrases in classical poetic usage. The work in Alers' form existed into the 19th century with the definitions as well as the entries written in Latin. Known to many generations of students throughout Europe, and passing through numerous editions, 19th century English-speaking schoolchildren knew the 1818 revision by Dr John Carey (1756–1826) simply as 'Carey's Gradus'. It was specially intended for the study and appreciation of Latin poetry of the classical period, and to aid students in the practice of verse composition.

=100  \\$aBredero, Gerbrand Adriaenszoon$d1585-1618$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560740$94858
=245  \\$aAlle de wercken, soo spelen, gedichten, brieven, kluchten en liederen
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bHoorn$c1678
=300  \\$a[xv]-732-[ii]-62 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=500  \\$aGerbrand Adriaenszoon Bredero (1585-1618) was a Dutch poet, playwright and 'rederijker', not of highly cultivated Renaissance literature but of a vernacular poetry. His most important work is the 1617 comedy 'Spaanschen Brabander'. His plays span three genres: farces, comedies and tragicomedies. His best-known farce is 'De klucht van de koe' from 1612. As a lyricist, he is best known for his 'Groot Liedboeck', published posthumously in 1622. Although he also wrote some successful sonnets, he had a particular aptitude for traditional song.

=041  \\$alat$heng
=100  \\$aBrowne, Thomas$cSir$d1605-1682$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q313925$97145
=245  \\$aReligio medici
=250  \\$a1st Latin ed.
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHack$c1644
=300  \\$a235-[4] pages$bfrontispiece engraving
=500  \\$aFirst book of Sir Thomas Browne (1605-1682), a doctor and polymath influenced by Francis Bacon's thought, but also struck by melancholy. It deals with the doctor's own Christian faith. As an autobiography, it is one of the very first of its kind. It was imitated numerous times, parodied (e.g., by John Dryden in his 'Religio Laici'), praised by Samuel Pepys and Virginia Woolf, and rediscovered by the Romantics in the nineteenth century (Coleridge in particular). It inspired Carl Gustav Jung to the term 'Religio Medici'.
=500  \\$aFamous frontispiece engraving depicting a person falling from a mountain into the sea, saved by the hand of God appearing through a cloud.
=500  \\$aManuscript annotations throughout the book: underlined passages, notes
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1642
=563  \\$aCardboard cover with red edges

=500  \\$aChristian Felix Weiße (1726–1804) a German writer and pedagogue, was among the leading representatives of the Enlightenment in Germany and is regarded as the founder of German children's literature. Four of his poems were set to music by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. His most lasting success were the librettos to Johann Adam Hiller's Singspiele.

=100  \\$aGoldoni, Carlo$d1707-1793$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q165534$911653
=245  \\$aScelte comedie$nvols. 1 & 2
=260  \\$aPadua$bBettoni$c1811
=300  \\$a2 vols. (332+284 pages)
=500  \\$aCarlo Osvaldo Goldoni (1707-1793) was an Italian playwright and librettist from the Republic of Venice. His works include some of Italy's most famous and best-loved plays. Audiences have admired the plays of Goldoni for their ingenious mix of wit and honesty. His plays offered his contemporaries images of themselves, often dramatizing the lives, values, and conflicts of the emerging middle classes. Though he wrote in French and Italian, his plays make rich use of the Venetian language, regional vernacular, and colloquialisms.
=500  \\$aGoldoni also wrote under the pen name and title Polisseno Fegeio, Pastor Arcade, which he claimed in his memoirs the "Arcadians of Rome" bestowed on him.
=500  \\$aThese are volumes 1 and 2 of a twelve-volume set

=245  \\$aDe levens en werken der Hollandsche en Vlaamsche kunstschilders, beeldhouwers, graveurs en bouwmeesters, van het begin der vijftiende eeuw tot heden $n1-3/3

=300  \\$a3 vols. in 1 (xxxii-viii-336-[1]-viii-308-[1] pages)$blithography on frontispiece, illustrations, portraits, leather bound, embossed spine, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aIn 1835, Immerzeel began to work on his magnum opus, a reference work on the lives and works of Dutch and Flemish painters, sculptors, engravers and master builders from 1500 to 1850. He incorporated existing biographies, but also used unpublished manuscripts and documents. Of the works, he listed the place where they were kept, and often the price, based on data from auctions and inventories. When he died in 1841, the work was completed by two sons, Charles Henri (1803-1878) and Christiaan (1808-1886), a painter. The three volumes were published in 1842 and 1843.
=500  \\$avol.1: A-G
vol.2: H-Q
vol.3: R-Z; monograms

=500  \\$aThe Epistle of Ignatius to the Romans (often abbreviated Ign. Rom.) is an epistle attributed to Ignatius of Antioch, a second-century bishop of Antioch. It was written during his transport from Antioch to his execution in Rome. To the Romans contains Ignatius’ most detailed explanation of his views on martyrdom. 
=500  \\$aTitle: "The genuine epistle of St. Ignatius. =041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aBentivoglio, Guido$d1577-1644$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1364155$97172
=245  \\$aHistoria di Fiandra del Cardinal Bentivoglio
=246  \1$aDella guerra di Fiandra Descritta dal Cardinal Bentvoglio
=260  \\$aVenice$bCiera$c1702
=300  \\$a3 vols. in 1 ([iv]-256-[12]-168-[8]-236-[11] pages)$bengraved title pages, illuminated initials, cardboard cover, leather gilt embossed spine
=500  \\$aGuido Bentivoglio d'Aragona was an Italian cardinal, statesman and historian.  He was an ecclesiastical diplomat at the court of the Archdukes Albert and Isabella in the Habsburg Netherlands (1607-1615), Bentivoglio was considered a lover of art and music. Immediately after his arrival in Flanders, he had the organist and composer Girolamo Frescobaldi (1583-1643) come to Brussels from Ferrara, where he was a celebrated musician and, with Bentivoglio's help, published his madrigals in Antwerp in 1608. It is considered certain that Bentivoglio also had contact with the artists there, such as Rubens. Later, too, he favoured Flemish artists in particular, such as Anthonis van Dyck and François Duquesnoy Il Fiammingo, by whom he was portrayed. 
=500  \\$aThe historical work Della guerra di Fiandra describes, in an eloquent style of great literary sophistication, the religious and civil wars in the Low Countries, which Bentivoglio observed with a keen eye, not only through direct experience during diplomatic missions there, but also through the direct involvement of no less than four brothers and two nephews.

=100  \\$aPlautus, Titus Maccius$d250 BC-164 BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q47160$94887
=245  \\$aComœdiæ

=260  \\$aLeiden$bHack$c1664
=300  \\$a[xvi]-1154-[[52] pages$bleather bound, gilded spine, engraved title page, marbled endpapers, red edges
=500  \\$aPlautus is known for his powerful, humorous and lively, original Latin style. He is primarily concerned with stage effect, not literary effect. Nor does he have any political commitment or social criticism. For his comedies, he used Attic (Greek) comedies as examples, but rendered them very freely and with many changes. Through the masterful use of the Latin vernacular, transposing the action to Roman states, inserting songs and merging pieces from different comedies, he managed to make the pieces into original creations that are cleverly put together. 
=500  \\$aPlautus probably wrote all his works between the last years of the Second Punic War and his death. The chronology of his works is partly unknown, so they are usually given in alphabetical order. 
=500  \\$aComplete edition of Plautus' 21 known Comedies,from Aphitruo to the fragments of Vidularia.
=500  \\$aExtraordinary title page engraving by P. Phil. decpicting a stage with 4 characters: a dressed monkey; a woman, a sater carying a globe, a warrior with shield and sword.

=100  \\$aBonarelli della Rovere, Guidubaldo$d1563-1608$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2376577$97177
=245  \\$aFillis van Scirus. $bHerderspel van den Grave G. De Bonarelli
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWor$bLinden, onder de$c1728
=300  \\$bfrontispiece engraving, engraved title page, illustrations$a[xvi]-285-[2] pages
=500  \\$aGuidubaldo Bonarelli wrote the pastoral drama 'Filli di Sciro' (published in 1607 but first performed in Ferrara four years earlier), a successful remake of the Leggenda di Florio e Biancofiore, whose musicality is a prelude to melodrama. The story of the drama is also intricate due to the overlapping of various love plots between the shepherd protagonists; in the end, the affair is resolved thanks to the mechanism of agnition. The genius of the plot, which struck and aroused much controversy among Bonarelli's contemporaries, was the character of the nymph in love with two shepherds, who meditated suicide because of her uncertainty. The play was a great success throughout the 17th century and was translated into French, English and Dutch
=500  \\$aTogether with Torquato Tasso's 'Aminta' and Giambattista Guarini's 'Il pastor fido', Bonarelli's 'Filli di Sciro' is considered one of the masterpieces of the genre of the pastoral drama
=500  \\$aPosthumous publication. After the author's death, Henrietta Elizabeth and Everardina Jakoba de With made sure that what remained of their sister's work was published. Thus, as early as 1728, Fillis van Scirus was published, supplemented by her Mengeldichten. The dedication of both sisters to Pieter Vlaming suggests that the latter had visited Katharina shortly before her death and that she had asked him to dedicate Fillis to him. 
=500  \\$aSecond part of the book contains ca.100 pages of poetry by de With (pastoral poems, fishermen's poems, funeral poems, and 'Mengeldichten')
=500  \\$aBound in with 'De getrouwe herderin' and ‘Gedichten’
=500  \\$aBeautiful full page illustrations at the start of each of the 5 acts, engraved by and after Jan Goeree (1670-1731)

=100  \\$aSachs, Johann Christian$d1720-1789$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1604120$97179
=245  \\$aEinleitung in die Geschichte der Marggravschaft und des marggrävlichen altfürstlichen Hauses Baden$nvol. 3
=260  \\$aKarlsruhe$bLotter$c1769
=300  \\$a[VIII]-686 pages
=500  \\$aJohann Christian Sachs was a grammar school rector at the gymnasium in Karlsruhe and a Protestant church councillor in the Margraviate of Baden. Sachs is also known as a historian of the House of Baden - especially for his German version of  'Historia Zaringo-Badensis' by Johann Daniel Schöpflin (1694-1771)
=500  \\$aAs early as 1754 - before Schöpflin had been commissioned by the Margrave to write a history of the House of Baden - Sachs began to publish lectures at the gymnasium on the origins of the House of Baden and on the lives of individual margraves from the 12th to the 16th centuries. From 1764 to 1773 he published his work in five volumes, which follows the systematics of Schöpflin's 'Historia' and is in parts a translation of this Latin work supplemented by his own annotations. The project was approved by Schöpflin. Sachs also drew on preliminary work by Johannes Gamans, Johann Friedrich Jüngler, Gabriel Förster, Karl Friedrich Drollinger, Friedrich Theobald Sahler and Jakob Friedrich Herbster.
=500  \\$aThe five volumes this Opus were published between 1764 and 1773

=245  \\$aAbhandlung vom sogenannten Pfeifer-Gerichts
=250  \\$a1st Ed.
=260  \\$aFrankfurt am Main$bMulz$c1752
=300  \\$a[xv]-248-[8] pages$bengraved frontispiece, multi-coloured endpapers and edges, leather bound, gilded spine
=500  \\$afrontispiece engraving  by  Joh. Mich. Eben (1716-1761) after I.H.H. Fries jun(ior) containing music, referring to specific pages in the book
=500  \\$ahttps://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pfeifergericht
=500  \\$aThe Pfeifergericht was a ceremony of the imperial city of Frankfurt am Main. It took place annually as part of a court day at the autumn fair and was first mentioned in a document in 1380. The origins of the ceremony lay in a privilege with which King Henry IV had exempted the citizens of Worms from the customs at Frankfurt in 1074. The customs duty was levied on all long-distance traders travelling north or east through the Frankfurt Main ford, and later also on merchants travelling to the Frankfurt Autumn Fair, which was documented from the middle of the 12th century. On the day before the Nativity of the Virgin Mary (on 7 September), the traditional start of the autumn fair, the 14 aldermen gathered in the Kaisersaal of the Römer under the chairmanship of the city sheriff to hold court. Meanwhile, the deputies of the three cities met in the Nuremberg Court. From there they moved over to the Römerberg. The procession was led by three Nuremberg city pipers who blew the traditional melody of the Piper's March on a shawm, a trombone and a pommer.

=500  \\$aDeals with witch hunts in the 17th century. The play is set in 1638 at the home of the mayor of Haarlem. A divided Europe and a divided Netherlands also divide minds in the mayor's home. Religion and science face each other, as well as collaboration and resistance, and finally inner certainty versus uncertainty.
=500  \\$aWritten in 1914 in honour of the opening of the Haarlem City Theatre. First performed in Amsterdam february 1915
=520  \\$aAt the beginning of the 17th century, Stadholder Frederick Henry is busy laying siege to Antwerp. At the time, the patriotic Cousaert is the bailiff of Haarlem. When he hears from Hille Babbe the fishwife that his son-in-law Arent, a young, wealthy Amsterdam merchant, is supplying arms and ammunition to Antwerp, he must make a choice: betray his son-in-law and thus grieve his daughter Estella or remain silent about this betrayal.

=300  \\$a189 pages$binserted original etch, cloth cover, embossed gilded letters with silver gauffered endpapers, gilt edges
=500  \\$aThe first volume was written and published in 1887, which is where Frederik van Eeden made his fame as a writer. Volume 2 appeared in 1905. Volume 3 in 1906.
=500  \\$aThe story centres on the development from child to adult and the struggle with life's riddles. The story is not just a fairy tale. It involves the following elements: the stages of human life; contrasts (good/evil, idealism/materialism); the diminutive motif; criticism of human society; the search for happiness; positivism and pantheism.


=500  \\$aTogether with Godfried Bomans' Erik or the little insect book, it was on the literature list of secondary schools in Belgium for many years. In the Netherlands, too, it is a widely read book that can be found on the reading lists of many secondary school teachers and schools.

=500  \\$aConlin began his literary activity in 1705. By 1711 he had written his seven-volume 'Fool's World'. With moralising and entertaining intentions, human behaviour is caricatured and illustrated by "more than 200 amusing and ridiculous incidents", "which can be usefully employed not only by the priests on the cantzel / but also by every private citizen / among honest societies". The series was concluded in 1709 and 1711 with two volumes on foolish women entitled Der Christliche Welt-Weise Beweinet Die Thorheit Derer in diesem Buch beschriebener 25. Närrinnen.

=500  \\$aCharles Collé (1709-1783) was a French dramatist and songwriter.
=500  \\$aThe 'Théâtre de société' is a collection of comedies published in 1768. It was namely for his patron, Louis Philippe I Duke of Orléans and his associates that Collé composed the greater part of his Théâtre de société. With this collection, Collé wanted to show the public his most elaborate pieces, in order to prove that he was capable of composing something other than parades, the genre in which he had become famous.

=520  \\$aSebastian Hensel, a great-grandson of the philosopher Moses Mendelssohn and son of Fanny Mendelssohn, wrote this family chronicle in 1879. The Mendelssohn family is a German-Jewish family of scholars, bankers and artists. For many years, the descendants remained connected through the joint management of the Mendelssohn banking house. Numerous artists also descended from the family - among them the famous composer, pianist and organist Felix Mendelssohn Bartholdy.
